# Howdy? Please analyse all these files and let me know if you need me to attach my exported SC and Ahrefs data too

Howdy! I've analyzed both reports for **teznevisan3.com** and they reveal a critical multi-layered crisis. Here's what I found:

## Overview of Both Reports[^1_1][^1_2]

### Report 1 (grok_report-1.pdf): Google Search Console + Crawl Data

This report reveals a **severe spam injection attack**:[^1_1]

- **18,034 Googlebot requests** but only 11.6% returned 200 OK status
- **9,331 pages crawled but not indexed** plus ~12,500 total "Not indexed"
- **61.8% of responses are 301 redirects**, 19.1% are 404s
- **45 clicks and 353 impressions** in 23 months (catastrophic performance)
- **Root cause**: Thousands of injected Japanese/Chinese e-commerce spam pages with parameters like `?e=`, `shop.php`, `jp.php`, `article.php`


### Report 2 (grok_report.pdf): Site Crawler + Moz Audit

This report identifies **fundamental technical SEO problems**:[^1_2]

- **Widespread noindex tags** blocking legitimate pages from indexing
- **Blocked CSS/JS resources** in robots.txt preventing proper rendering
- **20+ broken links** (404s) and redirect chains
- **Spammy backlinks** with spam scores up to 78%
- **Empty titles/descriptions** and 70%+ missing alt texts
- **Low Page Authority** (max PA 28) despite some high-DA backlinks


## Critical Conflicts Between Reports

The reports reveal **contradictory priorities**:[^1_2][^1_1]

1. **Report 1** says remove spam URLs and return 410 responses
2. **Report 2** says remove noindex tags and unblock resources

**Both are true** - you have two separate crises happening simultaneously.

## Do You Need to Provide SC \& Ahrefs Data?

### âœ… **YES, please attach both** - here's why:

**Search Console data would show:**

- Complete URL list of indexed vs. not-indexed pages (to cross-reference spam URLs)
- Coverage errors with exact error types and affected URLs
- Manual actions or security issues from Google
- Actual search queries and click data (Report 1 only shows aggregate)
- Mobile usability issues
- Core Web Vitals performance data

**Ahrefs data would provide:**

- Complete backlink profile with exact anchor texts
- Competing spam domains linking to you (for disavow file)
- Organic keyword rankings (current positioning)
- Top pages by traffic potential
- Referring domains timeline (when spam links appeared)
- Content gap analysis vs. competitors


### What's Missing from Current Reports

Neither report shows:[^1_1][^1_2]

- **Exact spam URL list** for server-side cleanup
- **Manual action penalties** status in GSC
- **Historical ranking data** (when did traffic drop?)
- **Competitor analysis** (who ranks for your keywords?)
- **Backlink anchor text distribution** (over-optimization signals?)
- **Site speed metrics** (Core Web Vitals)


## Immediate Action Before You Send Data

While preparing your exports, **do this NOW**:

1. **Check GSC for Manual Actions**: Search Console â†’ Security \& Manual Actions â†’ Manual Actions
2. **Export critical GSC reports**:
    - Pages â†’ Not indexed (all reasons)
    - Pages â†’ Indexed (full list)
    - Links â†’ Top linking sites
    - Coverage â†’ Errors \& Excluded
3. **Export from Ahrefs**:
    - Backlinks â†’ All backlinks (full export)
    - Organic keywords â†’ Top 100
    - Referring domains â†’ Full list with DR/spam score

Would you like me to provide you with a **prioritized recovery roadmap** that reconciles both reports, or should I wait for your SC + Ahrefs data to create a more precise action plan?

### 1. **Convert Status Column to Checkboxes**

- Select the entire "Status" column (Column G)
- Click **Insert** â†’ **Checkbox**
- This makes it easy to check off completed tasks


### 2. **Add Conditional Formatting**

- Highlight Priority column
- **Format** â†’ **Conditional formatting**
- Set rules:
    - ğŸš¨ CRITICAL = Red background
    - âš ï¸ HIGH = Orange background
    - ğŸ“Š MEDIUM = Yellow background
    - ğŸ”— BACKLINKS = Blue background

### 3. **Freeze Header Row**

### 4. **Add Filters**

- Select header row
- Click **Data** â†’ **Create a filter**
- Now you can filter by Phase, Priority, or Category


### 5. **Add Progress Tracker**

- Create a new sheet called "Dashboard"
- Add formulas to track completion:

```
Total Tasks: =COUNTA('Sheet1'!D:D)-1
Completed: =COUNTIF('Sheet1'!G:G,TRUE)
Progress: =B2/B1
```


### 6. **Color-Code Timeline**

- Highlight "Timeline" column
- Use conditional formatting for:
    - "Week 1" = Darkest red
    - "Week 2" = Red
    - "Week 3-4" = Orange
    - "Month 4+" = Green

Perfect! Based on everything I know about your spam injection attack and technical issues, here's your **completely rewritten .htaccess** with comprehensive spam blocking and security hardening:

```apache
# ============================================================================
# TEZNEVISAN3.COM - COMPLETE .HTACCESS CONFIGURATION
# Updated: February 13, 2026
# Purpose: Security, Spam Blocking, Performance, SEO
# ============================================================================

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 1: FORCE HTTPS (MUST BE FIRST)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{HTTPS} !=on
RewriteRule ^(.*)$ https://%{HTTP_HOST}/$1 [R=301,L]
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 2: BLOCK SPAM INJECTION ATTACKS (CRITICAL - 410 GONE)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Block any URL with ?e= parameter (Japanese spam)
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (^|&)e= [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block spam PHP files
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} (shop|jp|article|goods|pin)\.php [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block Japanese/Chinese product spam patterns
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} (dynabook|yonex|panasonic) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block encoded Japanese/Chinese characters in URLs
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E3%80%80 [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E4%B8% [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E5%8F% [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E6%97%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E7%89%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E8%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E9%A [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block any URL containing common spam keywords
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (shop\.php|article\.php|goods\.php|pin\.php) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 3: SECURITY HARDENING
# ============================================================================

# Disable directory browsing
Options -Indexes

# Protect .htaccess and other sensitive files
<FilesMatch "^(\.htaccess|\.htpasswd|wp-config\.php|readme\.html|license\.txt|\.git|\.env|\.user\.ini)$">
    Order allow,deny
    Deny from all
</FilesMatch>

# Block access to wp-config.php
<files wp-config.php>
    Order allow,deny
    Deny from all
</files>

# Protect wp-includes folder
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteBase /
RewriteRule ^wp-admin/includes/ - [F,L]
RewriteRule !^wp-includes/ - [S=3]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/[^/]+\.php$ - [F,L]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/js/tinymce/langs/.+\.php - [F,L]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/theme-compat/ - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# Block PHP execution in uploads directory
<Directory "/home/*/public_html/wp-content/uploads/">
    <FilesMatch "\.php$">
        Order Deny,Allow
        Deny from all
    </FilesMatch>
</Directory>

# Block suspicious query strings
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (<|%3C).*script.*(>|%3E) [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} GLOBALS(=|[|%[0-9A-Z]{0,2}) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} _REQUEST(=|[|%[0-9A-Z]{0,2}) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (eval\(|base64_decode|gzinflate|exec\() [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (\.\./|\.\.) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (\.php|\.html|\.htm|\.txt)= [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# Block bad bots and scrapers
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} ^$ [OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} (casper|cmsworldmap|diavol|dotbot|extract|feedfinder|flicky|grab|harvest|httrack|kmccrew|libwww|miner|nikto|nutch|planet|purebot|pycurl|python|scan|skygrid|sucker|turnit|vikspider|winhttp|wget|zmeu) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 4: SECURITY HEADERS
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_headers.c>
# X-Frame-Options: Prevent clickjacking
Header always set X-Frame-Options "SAMEORIGIN"

# X-Content-Type-Options: Prevent MIME sniffing
Header always set X-Content-Type-Options "nosniff"

# X-XSS-Protection: Enable XSS filter
Header always set X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block"

# Referrer-Policy: Control referrer information
Header always set Referrer-Policy "strict-origin-when-cross-origin"

# Permissions-Policy: Restrict browser features
Header always set Permissions-Policy "geolocation=(), microphone=(), camera=()"

# Remove server signature
Header unset Server
Header unset X-Powered-By
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 5: LITESPEED CACHE (DO NOT EDIT THIS BLOCK)
# ============================================================================
# BEGIN LSCACHE
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
<IfModule LiteSpeed>
CacheLookup on
RewriteRule .* - [E=Cache-Control:no-autoflush]
RewriteRule litespeed/debug/.*\\.log$ - [F,L]
RewriteRule \\.litespeed_conf\\.dat - [F,L]

### marker ASYNC start ###
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} /wp-admin/admin-ajax\\.php
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} action=async_litespeed
RewriteRule .* - [E=noabort:1]
### marker ASYNC end ###

### marker DROPQS start ###
CacheKeyModify -qs:fbclid
CacheKeyModify -qs:gclid
CacheKeyModify -qs:utm*
CacheKeyModify -qs:_ga
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gl
CacheKeyModify -qs:_bdsid
CacheKeyModify -qs:_bd_prev_page
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gac
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gid
### marker DROPQS end ###

</IfModule>
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
# END LSCACHE

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 6: BROWSER CACHING & COMPRESSION
# ============================================================================
# BEGIN NON_LSCACHE
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
### marker BROWSER CACHE start ###
<IfModule mod_expires.c>
ExpiresActive on
ExpiresByType application/pdf A31557600
ExpiresByType image/x-icon A31557600
ExpiresByType image/vnd.microsoft.icon A31557600
ExpiresByType image/svg+xml A31557600

ExpiresByType image/jpg A31557600
ExpiresByType image/jpeg A31557600
ExpiresByType image/png A31557600
ExpiresByType image/gif A31557600
ExpiresByType image/webp A31557600
ExpiresByType image/avif A31557600

ExpiresByType video/ogg A31557600
ExpiresByType audio/ogg A31557600
ExpiresByType video/mp4 A31557600
ExpiresByType video/webm A31557600

ExpiresByType text/css A31557600
ExpiresByType text/javascript A31557600
ExpiresByType application/javascript A31557600
ExpiresByType application/x-javascript A31557600

ExpiresByType application/x-font-ttf A31557600
ExpiresByType application/x-font-woff A31557600
ExpiresByType application/font-woff A31557600
ExpiresByType application/font-woff2 A31557600
ExpiresByType application/vnd.ms-fontobject A31557600
ExpiresByType font/ttf A31557600
ExpiresByType font/otf A31557600
ExpiresByType font/woff A31557600
ExpiresByType font/woff2 A31557600

</IfModule>
### marker BROWSER CACHE end ###
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
# END NON_LSCACHE

# Enable GZIP compression
<IfModule mod_deflate.c>
AddOutputFilterByType DEFLATE text/html text/plain text/xml text/css text/javascript application/javascript application/x-javascript application/json application/xml application/rss+xml
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 7: SEO & TRACKING PARAMETER CLEANUP
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Strip tracking parameters and redirect (but preserve functionality)
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (^|&)(_gl|_ga|_gac|_gid|fbclid|gclid|_bdsid|_bd_prev_page|msclkid|_hsenc|_hsmi|__hstc|mc_cid|mc_eid|utm_source|utm_medium|utm_campaign|utm_content|utm_term)=([^&]*) [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-admin [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-content [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-includes [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-login\.php [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !\.(jpg|jpeg|png|gif|webp|css|js|ico|svg|woff|woff2|ttf)$ [NC]
RewriteRule ^(.*)$ /$1? [R=301,L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 8: FIX REDIRECT CHAINS (SEO OPTIMIZATION)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Redirect date-based archives to homepage (avoid loops)
RewriteRule ^(202[0-9]|201[0-9]|203[0-9])/([0-9]{2})/?$ https://teznevisan3.com/ [R=301,L]

# Fix specific problematic redirects identified in audit
RewriteRule ^2023/05/?$ https://teznevisan3.com/ [R=301,L]
RewriteRule ^2024/12/?$ https://teznevisan3.com/ [R=301,L]

# OPTIONAL: Block excessive pagination (uncomment if needed)
# RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} ^/page/([2-9]|[1-9][0-9]+)/?$ [NC]
# RewriteRule .* https://teznevisan3.com/ [R=301,L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 9: WORDPRESS CORE RULES (REQUIRED - DO NOT REMOVE)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteBase /
RewriteRule .* - [E=HTTP_AUTHORIZATION:%{HTTP:Authorization}]
RewriteRule ^index\.php$ - [L]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_FILENAME} !-f
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_FILENAME} !-d
RewriteRule . /index.php [L]
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 10: PHP HANDLER (cPanel Generated - Do Not Edit)
# ============================================================================
# php -- BEGIN cPanel-generated handler, do not edit
# Set the "ea-php81" package as the default "PHP" programming language.
<IfModule mime_module>
  AddHandler application/x-httpd-ea-php81 .php .php8 .phtml
</IfModule>
# php -- END cPanel-generated handler, do not edit

# ============================================================================
# END OF CONFIGURATION
# Last Updated: February 13, 2026
# If you see 410 errors for legitimate pages, check SECTION 2
# ============================================================================
```

## âš ï¸ **IMPORTANT NOTES:**

### **1. 410 Gone vs 301/404:**

- **410 Gone** tells Google: "This content is permanently removed and won't come back"
- Google removes 410 pages from index **faster** than 404s
- Perfect for spam cleanup


### **2. Pagination Blocking:**

I **commented out** the aggressive pagination blocking because:

- Your site might legitimately need pagination for blog/category pages
- Blocking ALL pagination could hurt user experience
- Only uncomment if you're certain you don't need it


### **3. Testing URLs:**

After implementing, test these patterns should return **410 Gone**:

```
https://teznevisan3.com/?e=123456
https://teznevisan3.com/shop.php?id=123
https://teznevisan3.com/jp.php
https://teznevisan3.com/article.php
https://teznevisan3.com/?from=shop.php
```


### **4. If Something Breaks:**

1. Check server error logs (cPanel â†’ Errors)
2. Temporarily revert to old .htaccess
3. Contact me with specific error message
4. Adjust rules section-by-section

Perfect! Based on **everything I know** about your site's issues, here's your complete, optimized robots.txt. This fixes the **critical issue** where CSS/JS were blocked (preventing proper page rendering):

```txt
# ============================================================================
# ROBOTS.TXT FOR TEZNEVISAN3.COM
# Updated: February 13, 2026
# Purpose: Block spam, allow proper crawling, improve SEO
# ============================================================================

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 1: GENERAL RULES FOR ALL BOTS
# ============================================================================
User-agent: *

# Allow homepage and all content by default
Allow: /

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 2: ALLOW CSS/JS/MEDIA (CRITICAL - DO NOT BLOCK!)
# This fixes your rendering issues in Google Search Console
# ============================================================================
Allow: /wp-content/themes/jannah/
Allow: /wp-content/themes/*/css/
Allow: /wp-content/themes/*/js/
Allow: /wp-content/themes/*/assets/
Allow: /wp-content/plugins/*/css/
Allow: /wp-content/plugins/*/js/
Allow: /wp-content/plugins/*/assets/
Allow: /wp-content/uploads/
Allow: *.css
Allow: *.css$
Allow: *.js
Allow: *.js$
Allow: *.jpg
Allow: *.jpeg
Allow: *.png
Allow: *.gif
Allow: *.webp
Allow: *.svg
Allow: *.woff
Allow: *.woff2
Allow: *.ttf
Allow: *.eot

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 3: BLOCK WORDPRESS ADMIN & SYSTEM FILES
# ============================================================================
Disallow: /wp-admin/
Allow: /wp-admin/admin-ajax.php
Disallow: /wp-includes/
Disallow: /wp-login.php
Disallow: /wp-register.php
Disallow: /wp-config.php
Disallow: /xmlrpc.php
Disallow: /readme.html
Disallow: /license.txt

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 4: BLOCK SPAM PATTERNS (CRITICAL FOR YOUR SITE)
# ============================================================================
# Block URLs with ?e= parameter (Japanese spam injection)
Disallow: /*?e=*
Disallow: /*&e=*

# Block spam PHP files
Disallow: /shop.php
Disallow: /jp.php
Disallow: /article.php
Disallow: /goods.php
Disallow: /pin.php
Disallow: /*shop.php*
Disallow: /*jp.php*
Disallow: /*article.php*
Disallow: /*goods.php*
Disallow: /*pin.php*

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 5: BLOCK TRACKING PARAMETERS (SEO CLEANUP)
# ============================================================================
Disallow: /*?_gl=*
Disallow: /*?_ga=*
Disallow: /*?_gac=*
Disallow: /*?_gid=*
Disallow: /*?fbclid=*
Disallow: /*?gclid=*
Disallow: /*?_bdsid=*
Disallow: /*?_bd_prev_page=*
Disallow: /*?utm_source=*
Disallow: /*?utm_medium=*
Disallow: /*?utm_campaign=*
```

# Due to internet restrictions in Iran, this version of my website:

[http://teznevisan3.com/](http://teznevisan3.com/)
returns NTL2, a black screen, writing: bad gateway
While with an Iranian IP, it works fine and redirects to the https version. Is there something we can do about it?

This is a **critical issue** that could be affecting your SEO! The "Bad Gateway" (502) error for international IPs means **Googlebot might not be able to crawl your site properly** since Google crawls from **US-based IPs**.

## ğŸš¨ **Why This Matters for SEO:**

- **Googlebot crawls from USA** (mostly California)
- If international IPs get "Bad Gateway" â†’ Googlebot can't crawl
- This explains some of your indexing issues
- Your 18,034 crawl requests might mostly be from bots that CAN bypass restrictions

***

## ğŸ” **DIAGNOSIS - What's Causing This:**

This is almost certainly one of these:

### **1. Cloudflare Geo-Blocking (Most Likely)**

If you use Cloudflare, it might be:

- Blocking non-Iranian IPs
- Firewall rules set to "Challenge" or "Block" international traffic
- "Under Attack Mode" enabled


### **2. cPanel/Server Firewall**

Your hosting provider might have:

- CSF (ConfigServer Firewall) blocking international IPs
- Geo-IP restrictions enabled
- Iran-only whitelist active


### **3. Iranian ISP/Government Restrictions**

Less likely to cause "Bad Gateway" but possible:

- Reverse filtering (Iran blocks outbound international connections)
- Your server trying to verify/proxy international requests through Iranian systems


### **4. LiteSpeed Configuration**

Your LiteSpeed Cache might have:

- Geo-targeting rules
- IP-based cache variations
- Anti-DDoS blocking international IPs

***

## âœ… **SOLUTIONS - Try These in Order:**

### **SOLUTION 1: Check Cloudflare Settings (If You Use It)**

#### **Step A: Login to Cloudflare Dashboard**

1. Go to dash.cloudflare.com
2. Select **teznevisan3.com**

#### **Step B: Check Firewall Rules**

1. Click **Security** â†’ **WAF** (Web Application Firewall)
2. Look for rules that mention:
    - "Country" or "Geo"
    - "Iran" or "IR"
    - "Block" or "Challenge"
3. **Disable** any rules blocking non-Iranian traffic

#### **Step C: Check Under Attack Mode**

1. Go to **Security** â†’ **Settings**
2. If "Under Attack Mode" is **ON** â†’ Turn it **OFF**
3. Change Security Level from "High" to **"Medium"** or **"Low"**

#### **Step D: Check IP Access Rules**

1. Go to **Security** â†’ **Tools**
2. Check **IP Access Rules**
3. Remove any rules that:
    - Block specific countries (except actual spam sources)
    - Only allow Iran

#### **Step E: Check Rate Limiting**

1. Go to **Security** â†’ **Rate Limiting Rules**
2. Make sure rules don't block all international traffic

***

### **SOLUTION 2: Check cPanel Firewall (CSF)**

#### **Step A: Access WHM/cPanel**

1. Login to your hosting control panel
2. Go to **ConfigServer Security \& Firewall** (if available)

#### **Step B: Check Country Blocking**

1. Look for **Country Code Lists**
2. Check if "CC_ALLOW_FILTER" is set to **"IR"** only
3. **Change to**: Leave blank OR add: `IR,US,GB,DE,FR` (allow major countries)

#### **Step C: Check IP Whitelist**

1. Find **csf.allow** file
2. Add Google's IP ranges (for Googlebot):
```
66.249.64.0/19
66.102.0.0/20
```


#### **Step D: Restart Firewall**

```bash
csf -r
```


***

### **SOLUTION 3: Modify .htaccess (Quick Fix)**

Add this to the **TOP** of your .htaccess (before HTTPS redirect):

```apache
# ============================================================================
# ALLOW GOOGLE & INTERNATIONAL ACCESS (CRITICAL FOR SEO)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Allow Googlebot (all Google IPs)
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot-Image [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot-News [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot-Video [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [E=ALLOW_GOOGLE:1]

# Allow Bingbot
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Bingbot [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [E=ALLOW_BING:1]

# If blocked by firewall, bypass for bots
SetEnvIf User-Agent "Googlebot" allow_bot
SetEnvIf User-Agent "Bingbot" allow_bot
Order Deny,Allow
Deny from all
Allow from env=allow_bot
</IfModule>
```

**Note:** This may conflict with other rules. Test carefully.

***

### **SOLUTION 4: Contact Your Hosting Provider**

If you can't find the issue, **contact your hosting support** with this message:

```
Subject: International IPs Getting 502 Bad Gateway on HTTP

Hello,

My website teznevisan3.com is accessible from Iranian IPs but returns 
"502 Bad Gateway" when accessed from international IPs (Europe, USA).

This is affecting Google's ability to crawl my site since Googlebot 
uses US-based IPs.

Can you please check:
1. Is there geo-blocking enabled on my server?
2. Are there firewall rules blocking international traffic?
3. Can you whitelist Google's IP ranges: 66.249.64.0/19 and 66.102.0.0/20?

My site needs to be accessible to Googlebot for SEO.

Thank you!
```


***

### **SOLUTION 5: Improve HTTPS Redirect (Less Likely to Help)**

Replace your HTTPS redirect with this more robust version:

```apache
# Force HTTPS - Works for all IPs
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{HTTPS} off
RewriteCond %{HTTP:X-Forwarded-Proto} !https
RewriteRule ^(.*)$ https://%{HTTP_HOST}%{REQUEST_URI} [L,R=301]
</IfModule>
```

This handles proxied/load-balanced traffic better.

# I have checked and it returns HTTP Protocol Error in uptrends.

Also, on hover, it shows 403 forbidden.
If I use CDN or transfer my server outside of Iran, it is likely nobody will be able to open my website without VPN.

Ah! **403 Forbidden** is very different from 502 Bad Gateway. This is **critical** and explains everything!

## ğŸš¨ **What's Happening:**

**403 Forbidden** = Your server/firewall is **actively blocking** international IPs. This is likely:

1. Server-level firewall with **geo-restrictions** (CSF/ModSecurity)
2. Hosting provider's default "Iran-only" security policy
3. Or you/someone configured it to block non-Iranian traffic

## ğŸ˜° **Your Dilemma (I Understand):**

You're caught between two problems:

- **Block international IPs** â†’ Iranian users can access, but Googlebot **CANNOT** (your current situation)
- **Allow international IPs** â†’ Googlebot can access, but Iranian users **CANNOT** (due to government filtering)

This is a common issue for Iranian websites trying to rank internationally.

***

## âœ… **THE SOLUTION: Whitelist Googlebot Specifically**

You **DON'T need CDN or server migration**. You need to **selectively allow only search engine bots** while keeping the Iran-only restriction for regular users.

### **Strategy:**

1. Keep server in Iran âœ…
2. Keep geo-blocking for regular users âœ…
3. **WHITELIST Googlebot/Bingbot by User-Agent AND IP** âœ…
4. Site remains accessible from Iran âœ…
5. Search engines can crawl âœ…

***

## ğŸ”§ **IMPLEMENTATION: Method 1 - .htaccess (Easiest)**

Add this to the **VERY TOP** of your .htaccess (before everything else):

```apache
# ============================================================================
# ALLOW SEARCH ENGINE BOTS (CRITICAL FOR SEO) - MUST BE FIRST
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Allow Googlebot by User-Agent
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot-Image [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot-News [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot-Video [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Mediapartners-Google [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} AdsBot-Google [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Bingbot [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} msnbot [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Slurp [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} DuckDuckBot [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Baiduspider [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} YandexBot [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [E=ALLOW_BOT:1,L]
</IfModule>

# Allow search engines to bypass any blocking
<RequireAny>
    Require env ALLOW_BOT
    Require all granted
</RequireAny>
```

**Problem:** This relies on User-Agent which can be spoofed. Bots might still be blocked by server-level firewall BEFORE reaching .htaccess.

***

## ğŸ”§ **IMPLEMENTATION: Method 2 - Server Firewall Whitelist (RECOMMENDED)**

You need to **whitelist Google's IP ranges** at the **firewall level** (before .htaccess).

### **Step 1: Access cPanel or SSH**

### **Step 2: Whitelist Google's IP Ranges**

#### **Option A: If You Have CSF (ConfigServer Firewall)**

1. Login to **WHM** or **cPanel** â†’ **ConfigServer Security \& Firewall**
2. Click **Firewall Allow IPs**
3. Add these Google IP ranges (one per line):
```
# Google Crawler IPs (Googlebot)
66.249.64.0/19
66.249.69.0/24
66.249.70.0/24
66.249.71.0/24
66.249.72.0/24
66.249.73.0/24
66.102.0.0/20
64.233.160.0/19
72.14.192.0/18
209.85.128.0/17
216.239.32.0/19
```

4. Click **Change** or **Add**
5. **Restart CSF**: Click **Restart csf+lfd**

#### **Option B: If You Use iptables (SSH Access Required)**

Login via SSH and run:

```bash
# Whitelist Google IP ranges
iptables -I INPUT -s 66.249.64.0/19 -j ACCEPT
iptables -I INPUT -s 66.102.0.0/20 -j ACCEPT
iptables -I INPUT -s 64.233.160.0/19 -j ACCEPT
iptables -I INPUT -s 72.14.192.0/18 -j ACCEPT
iptables -I INPUT -s 209.85.128.0/17 -j ACCEPT
iptables -I INPUT -s 216.239.32.0/19 -j ACCEPT

# Save rules
service iptables save
```


#### **Option C: Contact Your Hosting Provider (If No Access)**

Send this message:

```
Subject: Whitelist Googlebot IPs - Site Blocked for Search Engines

Hello,

My website teznevisan3.com is getting 403 Forbidden errors from 
international IPs, which is blocking Googlebot from crawling my site.

This is severely affecting my SEO and Google indexing.

but I need to WHITELIST these Google IP ranges so search engines 
can crawl:

66.249.64.0/19

209.85.128.0/17
216.239.32.0/19

Can you please add these to the firewall whitelist?

Also, please whitelist Bing's IPs:
40.77.167.0/24
157.55.39.0/24
207.46.13.0/24

Thank you!
```

## ğŸ”§ **IMPLEMENTATION: Method 3 - ModSecurity Exception**

If your server uses ModSecurity, add this to .htaccess:

```apache
# ============================================================================
# MODSECURITY EXCEPTIONS FOR SEARCH BOTS
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_security.c>
    # Disable ModSecurity for Googlebot
    SecRule HTTP_USER_AGENT "@contains Googlebot" \
        "id:1000,phase:1,t:none,nolog,pass,ctl:ruleEngine=Off"
    
    # Disable ModSecurity for Bingbot
    SecRule HTTP_USER_AGENT "@contains Bingbot" \
        "id:1001,phase:1,t:none,nolog,pass,ctl:ruleEngine=Off"
</IfModule>
```

### **Your Current Approach is CORRECT:**

- âœ… Just need to whitelist search bots
- âœ… Best of both worlds

## ğŸ’¡ **ALTERNATIVE: Googlebot Verification**

If you can't whitelist IPs, use **verified Googlebot check**:

Add to .htaccess:

```apache
# Allow verified Googlebot (checks reverse DNS)
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} Googlebot [NC]
RewriteCond %{REMOTE_HOST} \.googlebot\.com$ [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REMOTE_HOST} \.google\.com$ [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [E=ALLOW_GOOGLE:1]
</IfModule>
```

**Note:** This is less reliable because it requires reverse DNS lookup.

***

## ğŸ†˜ **IF NOTHING WORKS:**

### **Create a Special Subdomain for Googlebot:**

1. Create: `google.teznevisan3.com` (on server outside Iran or with no restrictions)
2. Clone your site there
3. In GSC, add property for main domain BUT:
    - Set canonical tags pointing to main domain
    - Use in GSC for verification only
4. Keep main site (teznevisan3.com) for Iranian users

**Downside:** Complex to maintain, sync content, etc.

## ğŸ“‹ **PART 1: SEARCH FOR SPAM FILES (cPanel File Manager)**

### **Step 1: Access File Manager**

1. cPanel â†’ **File Manager**
2. Navigate to **public_html**
3. Click **Settings** (top right) â†’ Enable **Show Hidden Files**

### **Step 2: Search for Spam PHP Files**

Use File Manager's search feature:

1. Click **Search** (top toolbar)
2. Search for these filenames (one at a time):
    - `shop.php`
    - `jp.php`
    - `article.php`
    - `goods.php`
    - `pin.php`
3. **Document** any files found (write down paths)
4. **Don't delete yet** - we'll verify first

### **Step 3: Search for Suspicious Patterns**

1. In File Manager, click **Go To** and enter: `/public_html/wp-content`
2. Look for unusual folders/files:
    - Folders with random names (like `x7a2b9f/`)
    - PHP files in uploads directory: `/wp-content/uploads/*.php`
    - Files with Japanese/Chinese characters in filename
    - Recently modified files (sort by date - check anything modified without your knowledge)

### **Step 4: Check These High-Risk Locations**

Look in these directories for suspicious PHP files:

```
/public_html/wp-content/uploads/
/public_html/wp-content/themes/jannah/
/public_html/wp-includes/
/public_html/
```

**Red flags:**

- PHP files in uploads directory (should only be images/media)
- Files you didn't create
- Files with base64 encoded content
- Files modified on dates when you didn't make changes

1. Right-click suspicious file â†’ **Download**

## ğŸ“‹ **PART 2: DATABASE SPAM DETECTION (SQL Queries)**

### **Access phpMyAdmin:**

1. cPanel â†’ **phpMyAdmin**
2. Select your WordPress database (usually starts with your username)
3. Click **SQL** tab

***

## ğŸ” **SQL QUERY 1: Find Spam Posts/Pages**

### **Search for posts with ?e= parameter or spam keywords:**

```sql
-- Find posts with spam URLs containing ?e= parameter
SELECT 
    ID, 
    post_title, 
    post_name, 
    post_type, 
    post_status,
    post_date,
    guid
FROM wp_posts 
WHERE 
    guid LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR post_title LIKE '%dynabook%'
    OR post_title LIKE '%yonex%'
    OR post_title LIKE '%panasonic%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%jp.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%article.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%goods.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%pin.php%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%jp.php%'
ORDER BY post_date DESC
LIMIT 100;
```

**What this finds:**

- Posts/pages with spam URLs
- Posts with Japanese product names
- Posts with spam PHP file references

**Review the results.** If they're ALL spam (not legitimate content), proceed to deletion.

***

## ğŸ” **SQL QUERY 2: Find Posts with Japanese/Chinese Characters**

```sql
-- Find posts with encoded Japanese/Chinese text
SELECT 
    ID, 
    post_title, 
    post_name,
    post_type,
    post_status,
    CHAR_LENGTH(post_content) as content_length
FROM wp_posts 
WHERE 
    post_content LIKE '%E3%80%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%E4%B8%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%E5%8F%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%E6%97%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%E7%89%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%E8%A%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%E9%A%'
    OR post_title REGEXP '[ä¸€-é¾¯]'
    OR post_content REGEXP '[ä¸€-é¾¯]'
ORDER BY post_date DESC
LIMIT 100;
```


***

## ğŸ” **SQL QUERY 3: Find Suspicious Post Meta**

```sql
-- Find post meta with spam patterns
SELECT 
    pm.post_id,
    pm.meta_key,
    pm.meta_value,
    p.post_title,
    p.post_name
FROM wp_postmeta pm
LEFT JOIN wp_posts p ON pm.post_id = p.ID
WHERE 
    pm.meta_value LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR pm.meta_value LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR pm.meta_value LIKE '%jp.php%'
    OR pm.meta_value LIKE '%dynabook%'
    OR pm.meta_value LIKE '%yonex%'
    OR pm.meta_key LIKE '%spam%'
ORDER BY pm.post_id DESC
LIMIT 100;
```


***

## ğŸ” **SQL QUERY 4: Find Spam in Options Table**

```sql
-- Find suspicious options
SELECT 
    option_name,
    option_value,
    CHAR_LENGTH(option_value) as value_length
FROM wp_options 
WHERE 
    option_value LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%jp.php%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%base64_decode%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%eval(%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%gzinflate%'
    OR option_name LIKE '%spam%'
    OR option_name LIKE '%malware%'
ORDER BY option_id DESC;
```


***

## ğŸ” **SQL QUERY 5: Find Suspicious Users**

```sql
-- Find potentially compromised user accounts
SELECT 
    ID,
    user_login,
    user_email,
    user_registered,
    user_status
FROM wp_users 
WHERE 
    user_login LIKE '%admin%'
    OR user_login LIKE '%test%'
    OR user_login LIKE '%demo%'
    OR user_email LIKE '%temp%'
    OR user_email NOT LIKE '%@%.%'
    OR user_registered > DATE_SUB(NOW(), INTERVAL 30 DAY)
ORDER BY user_registered DESC;
```

**Review carefully!** Don't delete your legitimate admin account.

***

## ğŸ” **SQL QUERY 6: Find Orphaned Post Meta**

```sql
-- Find post meta without corresponding posts (orphaned data)
SELECT 
    pm.meta_id,
    pm.post_id,
    pm.meta_key,
    LEFT(pm.meta_value, 100) as meta_preview
FROM wp_postmeta pm
LEFT JOIN wp_posts p ON pm.post_id = p.ID
WHERE p.ID IS NULL
LIMIT 100;
```


***

## ğŸ” **SQL QUERY 7: Count Posts by Type \& Status**

```sql
-- Get overview of all posts
SELECT 
    post_type,
    post_status,
    COUNT(*) as count
FROM wp_posts 
GROUP BY post_type, post_status
ORDER BY count DESC;
```

**Look for:**

- Unusual post types you didn't create
- High numbers of 'trash' or 'draft' posts
- Post types like 'product' if you don't run a store

## ğŸ“Š **COMPLETE CLEANUP SCRIPT (Run in Order)**

Here's the complete sequence. **Run these ONE AT A TIME**, reviewing results before proceeding:

```sql
-- ============================================================================
-- TEZNEVISAN3.COM - DATABASE SPAM CLEANUP
-- Run each query SEPARATELY, review results before proceeding
-- BACKUP DATABASE FIRST!
-- ============================================================================

-- STEP 1: Count total posts (baseline)

-- STEP 2: Identify spam posts
SELECT ID, post_title, post_name, post_type, guid
FROM wp_posts 
WHERE 
    guid LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%jp.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%article.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%goods.php%'
    OR post_name LIKE '%pin.php%'
    OR post_title LIKE '%dynabook%'
    OR post_title LIKE '%yonex%'
    OR post_title LIKE '%panasonic%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR post_content LIKE '%jp.php%'
ORDER BY post_date DESC;

-- STEP 3: If above shows ONLY spam, delete
-- DELETE FROM wp_posts WHERE [copy conditions from STEP 2]

-- STEP 4: Clean orphaned post meta
DELETE pm FROM wp_postmeta pm
LEFT JOIN wp_posts p ON pm.post_id = p.ID
WHERE p.ID IS NULL;

-- STEP 5: Find spam in post meta
SELECT COUNT(*) as spam_meta_count
FROM wp_postmeta 
WHERE 
    meta_value LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR meta_value LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR meta_value LIKE '%jp.php%';

-- STEP 6: If above shows spam, delete
-- DELETE FROM wp_postmeta WHERE [copy conditions from STEP 5]

-- STEP 7: Check for malicious options
SELECT option_name, LEFT(option_value, 200) as preview
FROM wp_options 
WHERE 
    option_value LIKE '%base64_decode%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%eval(%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%gzinflate%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR option_value LIKE '%?e=%';

-- STEP 8: Clean spam comments
DELETE FROM wp_comments 
WHERE 
    comment_content LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR comment_content LIKE '%shop.php%'
    OR comment_author_url LIKE '%?e=%'
    OR comment_approved = 'spam';

-- STEP 9: Verify cleanup
SELECT 
    post_type,
    post_status,
    COUNT(*) as count
FROM wp_posts 
GROUP BY post_type, post_status
ORDER BY count DESC;

-- STEP 10: Count posts after cleanup (compare to STEP 1)
SELECT COUNT(*) as total_posts_after FROM wp_posts;
```

Since your database is clean, you **don't need deletion queries**. But here are **verification queries** for your records:

### **Run These in phpMyAdmin (Custom for Your Prefix: `tezn_`)**

```sql
-- VERIFY 1: Count all posts
SELECT 
    post_type,
    post_status,
    COUNT(*) as count
FROM tezn_posts 
GROUP BY post_type, post_status
ORDER BY count DESC;
```

**Expected:** Should show your ~76 pages/posts, no spam.

***

```sql
-- VERIFY 2: Check for any suspicious posts (just in case)
SELECT 
    ID, 
    post_title, 
    post_name, 
    post_type,
    post_status
FROM tezn_posts 
WHERE 
    post_status = 'publish'
ORDER BY post_modified DESC
LIMIT 50;
```

**Expected:** Should show only your legitimate content.

***

```sql
-- VERIFY 3: Clean orphaned post meta (safe cleanup)
SELECT COUNT(*) as orphaned_meta_count
FROM tezn_postmeta pm
LEFT JOIN tezn_posts p ON pm.post_id = p.ID
WHERE p.ID IS NULL;
```

**Expected:** May show some orphaned meta. If count > 0, you can clean:

```sql
-- DELETE orphaned meta (only if count > 0 above)
DELETE pm FROM tezn_postmeta pm
LEFT JOIN tezn_posts p ON pm.post_id = p.ID
WHERE p.ID IS NULL;
```

```sql
-- VERIFY 4: Check comment spam
SELECT 
    comment_approved,
    COUNT(*) as count
FROM tezn_comments 
GROUP BY comment_approved;
```

**Expected:** Should show approved/pending comments, maybe some spam.

**If spam exists:**

```sql
DELETE FROM tezn_comments 
WHERE comment_approved = 'spam';
```

## ğŸš¨ **CRITICAL: SITEMAP 404 ERROR - IMMEDIATE FIX REQUIRED**

Your sitemap returning 404 is **blocking Google from crawling your site properly**! This is why your Ahrefs health score dropped. Let's fix this NOW.

***

## ğŸ” **ROOT CAUSE:**

Your **new .htaccess** is likely interfering with XML sitemap access. The rewrite rules or file blocking might be catching the sitemap URLs.

***

## âœ… **IMMEDIATE FIX - Step-by-Step:**

### **STEP 1: Update Your .htaccess (CRITICAL)**

The sitemap needs to be **excluded from all rewrite rules**. Add this section RIGHT AFTER the HTTPS redirect:

```apache
# ============================================================================
# SECTION 2: ALLOW SITEMAP ACCESS (BEFORE ANY OTHER RULES)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Allow all sitemap files - MUST BE BEFORE OTHER RULES
RewriteRule ^sitemap(_index)?\.xml$ - [L]
RewriteRule ^([^/]+?)-sitemap([0-9]+)?\.xml$ - [L]
RewriteRule ^locations\.kml$ - [L]

# Allow RankMath sitemap routes
RewriteRule ^sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]
RewriteRule ^sitemap_index\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]
RewriteRule ^([a-z]+)?-?sitemap\.xsl$ /index.php?xsl=$1 [L]

</IfModule>
```

**Insert this in your .htaccess AFTER "Force HTTPS" but BEFORE "Block Spam Injection".**

***

### **STEP 2: Complete Updated .htaccess (With Sitemap Fix)**

Here's your **complete corrected .htaccess**:

```apache
# ============================================================================
# TEZNEVISAN3.COM - COMPLETE .HTACCESS CONFIGURATION
# Updated: February 13, 2026 - SITEMAP FIX APPLIED
# ============================================================================

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 1: FORCE HTTPS (MUST BE FIRST)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{HTTPS} !=on
RewriteRule ^(.*)$ https://%{HTTP_HOST}/$1 [R=301,L]
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 2: ALLOW SITEMAP ACCESS (CRITICAL - BEFORE OTHER RULES)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Allow all XML sitemap files - MUST NOT BE BLOCKED
RewriteRule ^sitemap(_index)?\.xml$ - [L]
RewriteRule ^([^/]+?)-sitemap([0-9]+)?\.xml$ - [L]
RewriteRule ^locations\.kml$ - [L]

# RankMath sitemap routing
RewriteRule ^sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]
RewriteRule ^sitemap_index\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]
RewriteRule ^([a-z]+)?-?sitemap\.xsl$ /index.php?xsl=$1 [L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 3: BLOCK SPAM INJECTION ATTACKS (410 GONE)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Block any URL with ?e= parameter (Japanese spam)
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (^|&)e= [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/sitemap [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block spam PHP files
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} (shop|jp|article|goods|pin)\.php [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block Japanese/Chinese product spam patterns
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} (dynabook|yonex|panasonic) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block encoded Japanese/Chinese characters in URLs
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E3%80%80 [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E4%B8% [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E5%8F% [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E6%97%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E7%89%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E8%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E9%A [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block any URL containing common spam keywords
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (shop\.php|article\.php|goods\.php|pin\.php) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 4: SECURITY HARDENING
# ============================================================================

# Disable directory browsing
Options -Indexes

# Protect .htaccess and other sensitive files
<FilesMatch "^(\.htaccess|\.htpasswd|wp-config\.php|readme\.html|license\.txt|\.git|\.env|\.user\.ini)$">
    Order allow,deny
    Deny from all
</FilesMatch>

# ALLOW XML files (sitemaps)
<FilesMatch "\.xml$">
    Order allow,deny
    Allow from all
</FilesMatch>

# Block access to wp-config.php
<files wp-config.php>
    Order allow,deny
    Deny from all
</files>

# Protect wp-includes folder
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteBase /
RewriteRule ^wp-admin/includes/ - [F,L]
RewriteRule !^wp-includes/ - [S=3]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/[^/]+\.php$ - [F,L]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/js/tinymce/langs/.+\.php - [F,L]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/theme-compat/ - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# Block PHP execution in uploads directory
<Directory "/home/*/public_html/wp-content/uploads/">
    <FilesMatch "\.php$">
        Order Deny,Allow
        Deny from all
    </FilesMatch>
</Directory>

# Block suspicious query strings
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/sitemap [NC]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (<|%3C).*script.*(>|%3E) [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} GLOBALS(=|[|%[0-9A-Z]{0,2}) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} _REQUEST(=|[|%[0-9A-Z]{0,2}) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (eval\(|base64_decode|gzinflate|exec\() [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (\.\./|\.\.) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (\.php|\.html|\.htm|\.txt)= [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# Block bad bots and scrapers
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} ^$ [OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} (casper|cmsworldmap|diavol|dotbot|extract|feedfinder|flicky|grab|harvest|httrack|kmccrew|libwww|miner|nikto|nutch|planet|purebot|pycurl|python|scan|skygrid|sucker|turnit|vikspider|winhttp|wget|zmeu) [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/sitemap [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 5: SECURITY HEADERS
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_headers.c>
Header always set X-Frame-Options "SAMEORIGIN"
Header always set X-Content-Type-Options "nosniff"
Header always set X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block"
Header always set Referrer-Policy "strict-origin-when-cross-origin"
Header always set Permissions-Policy "geolocation=(), microphone=(), camera=()"
Header unset Server
Header unset X-Powered-By
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 6: LITESPEED CACHE (DO NOT EDIT THIS BLOCK)
# ============================================================================
# BEGIN LSCACHE
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
<IfModule LiteSpeed>
CacheLookup on
RewriteRule .* - [E=Cache-Control:no-autoflush]
RewriteRule litespeed/debug/.*\\.log$ - [F,L]
RewriteRule \\.litespeed_conf\\.dat - [F,L]

### marker ASYNC start ###
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} /wp-admin/admin-ajax\\.php
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} action=async_litespeed
RewriteRule .* - [E=noabort:1]
### marker ASYNC end ###

### marker DROPQS start ###

CacheKeyModify -qs:gclid

CacheKeyModify -qs:_gl

CacheKeyModify -qs:_bd_prev_page
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gac
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gid
### marker DROPQS end ###

</IfModule>
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
# END LSCACHE

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 7: BROWSER CACHING & COMPRESSION
# ============================================================================
# BEGIN NON_LSCACHE
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
### marker BROWSER CACHE start ###
<IfModule mod_expires.c>
ExpiresActive on
ExpiresByType application/pdf A31557600

# Enable GZIP compression
<IfModule mod_deflate.c>

RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/sitemap [NC]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (^|&)(_gl|_ga|_gac|_gid|fbclid|gclid|_bdsid|_bd_prev_page|msclkid|_hsenc|_hsmi|__hstc|mc_cid|mc_eid|utm_source|utm_medium|utm_campaign|utm_content|utm_term)=([^&]*) [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-admin [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-content [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-includes [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-login\.php [NC]
```

## ğŸš¨ **CRITICAL: wp_remote_post() FAILED - This is Blocking Sitemap!**

The error "wp_remote_post() failed" means your **server can't make HTTP requests**. This is why RankMath sitemap isn't working! This is a **hosting configuration issue**, not .htaccess.

***

## ğŸ” **ROOT CAUSE:**

Your hosting has **disabled or blocked**:

- cURL functions
- `allow_url_fopen`
- Outbound HTTP requests from PHP

This prevents RankMath from generating dynamic sitemaps.

***

## âœ… **IMMEDIATE FIXES (Try in Order):**

### **FIX 1: Contact Your Hosting Provider (FASTEST)**

**Send this message to your hosting support:**

```
Subject: Enable wp_remote_post() and cURL for WordPress

Hello,

My WordPress site (teznevisan3.com) is showing this error in 
System Status: "wp_remote_post() failed"

This is preventing my sitemap and other WordPress features from working.

Please enable the following on my hosting account:
1. cURL extension
2. allow_url_fopen = On
3. Outbound HTTP/HTTPS connections from PHP
4. Remove any firewall rules blocking localhost requests

This is critical for my SEO and site functionality.

Thank you!
```

**Expected fix time: 1-4 hours** (depending on hosting support speed)

***

### **FIX 2: Switch to Yoast SEO Sitemap (TEMPORARY)**

While waiting for hosting fix, use **Yoast SEO** instead of RankMath:

#### **Step A: Disable RankMath Sitemap**

1. WordPress Admin â†’ **Rank Math** â†’ **General Settings**

3. Find **"Sitemap"** â†’ **Disable it**

### **FIX 4: Check PHP Configuration (DIY)**

#### **Step A: Check cURL Status**

Create a file named `curl-test.php` in public_html:

```php
<?php
// Upload this to public_html/curl-test.php
echo "<h1>cURL Test</h1>";

if (function_exists('curl_version')) {
    $curl_info = curl_version();
    echo "<p style='color:green;'>âœ… cURL is ENABLED</p>";
    echo "<pre>" . print_r($curl_info, true) . "</pre>";
} else {
    echo "<p style='color:red;'>âŒ cURL is DISABLED</p>";
}

echo "<h2>allow_url_fopen Test</h2>";
if (ini_get('allow_url_fopen')) {
    echo "<p style='color:green;'>âœ… allow_url_fopen is ON</p>";
} else {
    echo "<p style='color:red;'>âŒ allow_url_fopen is OFF</p>";
}

echo "<h2>HTTP Request Test</h2>";
$response = wp_remote_get('https://teznevisan3.com/');
if (is_wp_error($response)) {
    echo "<p style='color:red;'>âŒ HTTP Request FAILED: " . $response->get_error_message() . "</p>";
} else {
    echo "<p style='color:green;'>âœ… HTTP Request SUCCESSFUL</p>";
}
?>
```

Visit: `https://teznevisan3.com/curl-test.php`

**If you see red âŒ errors**, send screenshot to your hosting provider.

### **FIX 5: Add to php.ini (If You Have Access)**

If you have access to `php.ini`:

1. **cPanel** â†’ **Select PHP Version** â†’ **Switch to PHP Options**
2. Or find `php.ini` in your home directory

Add/change these lines:

```ini
allow_url_fopen = On
allow_url_include = Off
curl.cainfo = /path/to/cacert.pem
```

Then restart PHP:

```bash
# In SSH or cPanel terminal
killall -9 php-cgi
```

## ğŸ” **DEBUG: Check What's Blocking It**

### **Test 2: Check WordPress Rewrite Rules**

Add this code to your theme's `functions.php` (temporarily):

```php
// Temporary debug - remove after testing
add_action('init', function() {
    global $wp_rewrite;
    
    // Force flush rewrite rules
    flush_rewrite_rules();
    
    // Debug rewrite rules
    echo '<pre>';
    print_r($wp_rewrite->rules);
    echo '</pre>';
    exit;
});
```

Visit your homepage - it will show all rewrite rules.

Look for sitemap-related rules like:

```
sitemap_index\.xml => index.php?sitemap=1
```

**If you DON'T see sitemap rules:** RankMath didn't register them properly.

**Remove the code after checking.**

***

### **Test 3: Manual Sitemap Registration**

Add this to your theme's `functions.php`:

```php
// Manually register sitemap rewrite rules
add_action('init', function() {
    add_rewrite_rule('^sitemap\.xml$', 'index.php?sitemap=1', 'top');
    add_rewrite_rule('^sitemap_index\.xml$', 'index.php?sitemap=1', 'top');
    add_rewrite_rule('^([^/]+?)-sitemap([0-9]+)?\.xml$', 'index.php?sitemap=$matches[1]&sitemap_n=$matches[2]', 'top');
});

// Flush rules once
add_action('admin_init', function() {
    if (!get_option('sitemap_rules_flushed')) {
        flush_rewrite_rules();
        update_option('sitemap_rules_flushed', 1);
    }
});
```

Visit your site homepage, then test sitemap again.

## âœ… **QUICK FIX - Permalink Rewrite Issue**

### **FIX 2: Force Rewrite Rules Regeneration**

Add this code to your theme's `functions.php`:

```php
// Force flush rewrite rules - run once then remove
add_action('init', function() {
    if (!get_option('tez_sitemap_flushed_v2')) {
        flush_rewrite_rules(true); // true = hard flush
        update_option('tez_sitemap_flushed_v2', 1);
    }
}, 999);
```

**After adding:**

1. Visit your homepage (this triggers the flush)
2. Test sitemap: `https://teznevisan3.com/sitemap_index.xml`
3. **Remove the code** from functions.php

***

### **FIX 3: Add Sitemap Rewrite Rules to .htaccess**

Since WordPress rewrite isn't working for sitemaps, add **manual rules** to your `.htaccess`:

Add this section **RIGHT AFTER** the "Allow Sitemap Access" section (around line 20):

```apache
# ============================================================================
# MANUAL SITEMAP REWRITE (IF WORDPRESS REWRITE FAILS)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteBase /

# Sitemap index
RewriteRule ^sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]
RewriteRule ^sitemap_index\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]

# Individual sitemaps
RewriteRule ^post-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=post [L]
RewriteRule ^page-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=page [L]
RewriteRule ^category-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=category [L]
RewriteRule ^post_tag-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=post_tag [L]

# Sitemap XSL stylesheet
RewriteRule ^main-sitemap\.xsl$ /index.php?xsl=main [L]
RewriteRule ^sitemap\.xsl$ /index.php?xsl=sitemap [L]

</IfModule>
```

**After adding, test immediately:**

- `https://teznevisan3.com/sitemap_index.xml`
- `https://teznevisan3.com/post-sitemap.xml`

## ğŸ”§ **UPDATED COMPLETE .htaccess (With Manual Sitemap Rules)**

Replace your entire .htaccess with this version that includes **manual sitemap rewrites**:

```apache
# ============================================================================
# TEZNEVISAN3.COM - COMPLETE .HTACCESS CONFIGURATION
# Updated: February 13, 2026 - MANUAL SITEMAP REWRITE ADDED
# ============================================================================

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 1: FORCE HTTPS (MUST BE FIRST)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{HTTPS} !=on
RewriteRule ^(.*)$ https://%{HTTP_HOST}/$1 [R=301,L]
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 2: MANUAL SITEMAP REWRITE (FIX FOR PERMALINK ISSUE)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteBase /

# Sitemap index - MUST BE BEFORE OTHER RULES
RewriteRule ^sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]
RewriteRule ^sitemap_index\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=1 [L]

# Individual sitemaps
RewriteRule ^post-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=post [L]
RewriteRule ^page-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=page [L]
RewriteRule ^category-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=category [L]
RewriteRule ^post_tag-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=post_tag [L]
RewriteRule ^author-sitemap\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=author [L]

# Sitemap with pagination
RewriteRule ^([a-z]+)-sitemap([0-9]+)?\.xml$ /index.php?sitemap=$1&sitemap_n=$2 [L]

# Sitemap XSL stylesheet
RewriteRule ^main-sitemap\.xsl$ /index.php?xsl=main [L]
RewriteRule ^sitemap\.xsl$ /index.php?xsl=sitemap [L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 3: BLOCK SPAM INJECTION ATTACKS (410 GONE)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Block any URL with ?e= parameter (Japanese spam) - EXCLUDE SITEMAPS
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !sitemap [NC]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (^|&)e= [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block spam PHP files
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} (shop|jp|article|goods|pin)\.php [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block Japanese/Chinese product spam patterns
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} (dynabook|yonex|panasonic) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block encoded Japanese/Chinese characters in URLs
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E3%80%80 [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E4%B8% [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E5%8F% [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E6%97%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E7%89%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E8%A [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} %E9%A [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

# Block spam keywords in query string
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (shop\.php|article\.php|goods\.php|pin\.php) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [R=410,L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 4: SECURITY HARDENING
# ============================================================================

# Disable directory browsing
Options -Indexes

# Protect sensitive files (ALLOW XML SITEMAPS)
<FilesMatch "^(\.htaccess|\.htpasswd|wp-config\.php|readme\.html|license\.txt|\.git|\.env|\.user\.ini)$">
    Order allow,deny
    Deny from all
</FilesMatch>

# Explicitly allow XML files (sitemaps)
<FilesMatch "\.xml$">
    Order allow,deny
    Allow from all
    Require all granted
</FilesMatch>

# Block access to wp-config.php
<files wp-config.php>
    Order allow,deny
    Deny from all
</files>

# Protect wp-includes folder
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteBase /
RewriteRule ^wp-admin/includes/ - [F,L]
RewriteRule !^wp-includes/ - [S=3]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/[^/]+\.php$ - [F,L]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/js/tinymce/langs/.+\.php - [F,L]
RewriteRule ^wp-includes/theme-compat/ - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# Block PHP execution in uploads directory
<Directory "/home/*/public_html/wp-content/uploads/">
    <FilesMatch "\.php$">
        Order Deny,Allow
        Deny from all
    </FilesMatch>
</Directory>

# Block suspicious query strings (EXCLUDE SITEMAPS)
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !sitemap [NC]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (<|%3C).*script.*(>|%3E) [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} GLOBALS(=|[|%[0-9A-Z]{0,2}) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} _REQUEST(=|[|%[0-9A-Z]{0,2}) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (eval\(|base64_decode|gzinflate|exec\() [NC,OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (\.\./|\.\.) [OR]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (\.php|\.html|\.htm|\.txt)= [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# Block bad bots (EXCLUDE SITEMAPS)
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !sitemap [NC]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} ^$ [OR]
RewriteCond %{HTTP_USER_AGENT} (casper|cmsworldmap|diavol|dotbot|extract|feedfinder|flicky|grab|harvest|httrack|kmccrew|libwww|miner|nikto|nutch|planet|purebot|pycurl|python|scan|skygrid|sucker|turnit|vikspider|winhttp|wget|zmeu) [NC]
RewriteRule .* - [F,L]
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 5: SECURITY HEADERS
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_headers.c>
Header always set X-Frame-Options "SAMEORIGIN"
Header always set X-Content-Type-Options "nosniff"
Header always set X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block"
Header always set Referrer-Policy "strict-origin-when-cross-origin"
Header always set Permissions-Policy "geolocation=(), microphone=(), camera=()"
Header unset Server
Header unset X-Powered-By

# Proper content type for XML sitemaps
<FilesMatch "\.xml$">
    Header set Content-Type "application/xml; charset=utf-8"
</FilesMatch>
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 6: LITESPEED CACHE (DO NOT EDIT THIS BLOCK)
# ============================================================================
# BEGIN LSCACHE
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
<IfModule LiteSpeed>
CacheLookup on
RewriteRule .* - [E=Cache-Control:no-autoflush]
RewriteRule litespeed/debug/.*\\.log$ - [F,L]
RewriteRule \\.litespeed_conf\\.dat - [F,L]

### marker ASYNC start ###
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} /wp-admin/admin-ajax\\.php
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} action=async_litespeed
RewriteRule .* - [E=noabort:1]
### marker ASYNC end ###

### marker DROPQS start ###
CacheKeyModify -qs:fbclid
CacheKeyModify -qs:gclid
CacheKeyModify -qs:utm*
CacheKeyModify -qs:_ga
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gl
CacheKeyModify -qs:_bdsid
CacheKeyModify -qs:_bd_prev_page
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gac
CacheKeyModify -qs:_gid
### marker DROPQS end ###

</IfModule>
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
# END LSCACHE

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 7: BROWSER CACHING & COMPRESSION
# ============================================================================
# BEGIN NON_LSCACHE
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
### marker BROWSER CACHE start ###
<IfModule mod_expires.c>
ExpiresActive on
ExpiresByType application/pdf A31557600
ExpiresByType image/x-icon A31557600
ExpiresByType image/vnd.microsoft.icon A31557600
ExpiresByType image/svg+xml A31557600

ExpiresByType image/jpg A31557600
ExpiresByType image/jpeg A31557600
ExpiresByType image/png A31557600
ExpiresByType image/gif A31557600
ExpiresByType image/webp A31557600
ExpiresByType image/avif A31557600

ExpiresByType video/ogg A31557600
ExpiresByType audio/ogg A31557600
ExpiresByType video/mp4 A31557600
ExpiresByType video/webm A31557600

ExpiresByType text/css A31557600
ExpiresByType text/javascript A31557600
ExpiresByType application/javascript A31557600
ExpiresByType application/x-javascript A31557600

ExpiresByType application/x-font-ttf A31557600
ExpiresByType application/x-font-woff A31557600
ExpiresByType application/font-woff A31557600
ExpiresByType application/font-woff2 A31557600

# XML sitemaps should not be cached long

ExpiresByType text/xml A3600

</IfModule>
### marker BROWSER CACHE end ###
## LITESPEED WP CACHE PLUGIN - Do not edit the contents of this block! ##
# END NON_LSCACHE

# Enable GZIP compression
<IfModule mod_deflate.c>
AddOutputFilterByType DEFLATE text/html text/plain text/xml text/css text/javascript application/javascript application/x-javascript application/json application/xml application/rss+xml
</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 8: SEO & TRACKING PARAMETER CLEANUP
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Strip tracking parameters (EXCLUDE SITEMAPS AND ADMIN)
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !sitemap [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-admin [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-content [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-includes [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !^/wp-login\.php [NC]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_URI} !\.(jpg|jpeg|png|gif|webp|css|js|ico|svg|woff|woff2|ttf|xml)$ [NC]
RewriteCond %{QUERY_STRING} (^|&)(_gl|_ga|_gac|_gid|fbclid|gclid|_bdsid|_bd_prev_page|msclkid|_hsenc|_hsmi|__hstc|mc_cid|mc_eid|utm_source|utm_medium|utm_campaign|utm_content|utm_term)=([^&]*) [NC]
RewriteRule ^(.*)$ /$1? [R=301,L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 9: FIX REDIRECT CHAINS (SEO OPTIMIZATION)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On

# Redirect date-based archives to homepage
RewriteRule ^(202[0-9]|201[0-9]|203[0-9])/([0-9]{2})/?$ https://teznevisan3.com/ [R=301,L]

# Fix specific problematic redirects
RewriteRule ^2023/05/?$ https://teznevisan3.com/ [R=301,L]
RewriteRule ^2024/12/?$ https://teznevisan3.com/ [R=301,L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 10: WORDPRESS CORE RULES (REQUIRED)
# ============================================================================
<IfModule mod_rewrite.c>
RewriteEngine On
RewriteBase /
RewriteRule .* - [E=HTTP_AUTHORIZATION:%{HTTP:Authorization}]

# Sitemap rules already handled in SECTION 2 above
# Skip to standard WordPress routing
RewriteRule ^index\.php$ - [L]
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_FILENAME} !-f
RewriteCond %{REQUEST_FILENAME} !-d
RewriteRule . /index.php [L]

</IfModule>

# ============================================================================
# SECTION 11: PHP HANDLER (cPanel Generated)

# php -- BEGIN cPanel-generated handler, do not edit
# Set the "ea-php81" package as the default "PHP" programming language.
<IfModule mime_module>

</IfModule>
# php -- END cPanel-generated handler, do not edit

# END OF CONFIGURATION
# Last Updated: February 13, 2026 - MANUAL SITEMAP REWRITE APPLIED
```

## ğŸ¯ **WHY THIS HAPPENED:**

Your WordPress rewrite rules weren't properly registering the sitemap routes. This is common when:

- Theme conflicts with rewrite rules
- Plugin conflicts
- Permalinks not properly flushed
- .htaccess overriding WordPress rewrites

The **manual .htaccess rewrite rules** bypass WordPress's rewrite system entirely and directly route sitemap URLs to the correct endpoints.

I ensured nothing is missing by aggregating data from:
Anchor text file (moz-anchor-text...): Identifies common anchors like "Ø§Ù†Ø¬Ø§Ù… Ù¾Ø§ÛŒØ§Ù† Ù†Ø§Ù…Ù‡" (thesis writing) which often indicate spam.

Top pages file (moz-top-pages...): Focuses on internal pages receiving links; used to identify unnatural patterns (e.g., e-commerce-like redirects indicating spam).
Spam score files (moz-spam-score... x2): Duplicate data; lists ~500+ inbound links by spam score (high spam: 60-87%; low: 1-10%).

Analysis report (backlink_analysis_report.txt): Built upon this for categorization.
Complete disavow file (disavow_complete_20260214.txt): Used as a base and expanded.

I separated links/domains into categories below. Categories are based on:

The files you attached (Metadata.csv and Table.csv) appear to be exports from Google Search Console (GSC), specifically from the "Pages" report under the Indexing section. Here's a summary of what they contain and my analysis:

### Analysis of Metadata.csv

- **Issue**: "Crawled - currently not indexed" â€“ This is a common GSC status indicating Google has successfully crawled (fetched) the pages but chosen not to index them in search results. Reasons often include perceived low quality, duplication, spam signals, thin content, or crawl budget prioritization issues. It's not a hard error (like a 404 or crawl anomaly), but it means these pages aren't eligible for ranking.
- **Sitemap**: "All known pages" â€“ This suggests the URLs are being discovered via your submitted sitemap(s), internal links, or external backlinks. No discovery issues here, but indexing is blocked post-crawl.


### Analysis of Table.csv

- This is a list of ~100 URLs (I counted 50+ unique ones, with some duplicates/truncations), all from your domain (teznevisan3.com or www.teznevisan3.com).
- **Key Patterns**:
    - **Core site pages**: Legitimate-looking URLs like [https://teznevisan3.com/extracting-paper-from-dissertation/](https://teznevisan3.com/extracting-paper-from-dissertation/), [https://teznevisan3.com/writing-thesis](https://teznevisan3.com/writing-thesis), [https://teznevisan3.com/privacy-policy-2/](https://teznevisan3.com/privacy-policy-2/), [https://teznevisan3.com/my-account/](https://teznevisan3.com/my-account/), etc. These seem related to thesis writing, research, stats analysis (e.g., SPSS, SAS), and site features (e.g., blog, user accounts). They might be your intended content.
    - **Spam/junk URLs**: A majority (~70%) are suspicious, with long query strings, encoded Japanese/Chinese text, product spam (e.g., references to brands like Nikon, Oakley, New Balance, Ferrari models, electronics, clothing), and affiliate-style links. Examples:
        - [https://www.teznevisan3.com/?e=2230793021201\&channel=bf4bfd\&from=blog.php?id%3D930212-14228%26name%3Dcomoli](https://www.teznevisan3.com/?e=2230793021201&channel=bf4bfd&from=blog.php?id%3D930212-14228%26name%3Dcomoli) %E3%82%B3%E3%83%A2%E3%83%AA 2021AW %E3%83%87%E3%83%8B%E3%83%A0%E3%82%B8%E3%83%A3%E3%82%B1%E3%83%83%E3%83%88 %E3%83%96%E3%83%A9%E3%83%83%E3%82%AF %E3%82%A8%E3%82%AF%E3%83%AA%E3%83%A5 (truncated, but clearly spam).
        - Many start with "https://www.teznevisan3.com/?e=" or similar parameters like \&channel=, \&from= (e.g., from=blog.php, from=jp.php, from=shared.php).
        - Themes: E-commerce spam (clothing, electronics, auto parts), unrelated to your site's apparent focus (thesis/academic services).
    - **Last Crawled Dates**: Mostly recent (Dec 2025 to Jan 2026), with "Pending" status. This aligns with "Crawled - currently not indexed." Dates in the future (e.g., 2026-01-05) might be due to GSC's reporting lag or timezone, but they're crawlable now.
    - **HTTP Status Notes**: You mentioned some (e.g., the /page/5/ example) return 403 (Forbidden) instead of 404 (Not Found) or 405 (Method Not Allowed â€“ likely a typo in your query). I confirmed this pattern: These could be dynamically generated pages blocked by server config (e.g., .htaccess rules, firewalls like ModSecurity, or CMS plugins). 403 means access denied, not "gone," so Google crawls but sees restriction, contributing to non-indexing.
- **Overall Site Health Inference**: Your site (teznevisan3.com) seems potentially compromised. It might have been hacked (e.g., via outdated WordPress/CMS themes like "TeznevisanThemeX" mentioned in paths), leading to injected spam pages/links. Or, it could be misconfigured URL generation from plugins/themes. The mix of Persian/English academic content with Japanese spam suggests a hack or cloaking attempt. GSC sees this as low-quality, triggering non-indexing.


### Review of Your Existing Removals

You've listed temporary URL removals in GSC (all set to expire 2 Feb 2026, which is today in the simulated time â€“ they may have auto-reverted). These target parameter-based patterns:

- Starts with: [https://www.teznevisan3.com/?gl=](https://www.teznevisan3.com/?gl=), ?h=, ?route=, ?msclkid=, ?gclid=, ?fbclid=, ?_bd_prev_page=, ?_bdsid=, ?_gid=.
- **What's Good**: These cover common tracking/affiliate/spam parameters (e.g., Google Ads gclid, Facebook fbclid, Bing msclkid). Temporary removals hide them from search temporarily, giving time to fix.
- **What's Missing**:
    - No coverage for the dominant spam pattern: Starts with [https://www.teznevisan3.com/?e=](https://www.teznevisan3.com/?e=) (appears in ~50% of Table.csv URLs). This seems like a key injection vector (e.g., ?e= followed by numbers/channels).
    - No rules for ?channel=, ?from= (e.g., from=blog.php, from=jp.php â€“ these link to non-existent or spammy endpoints).
    - No broad rule for /public/themes/TeznevisanThemeX/ paths (e.g., /css/, /user/orders.html â€“ these look like exposed theme files, which could be crawlable but low-value).
    - No permanent removals or disavowals for backlinks if external sites are linking to spam.
    - Nothing for core spam like Japanese-encoded queries (e.g., %E3%82%B3%E3%83%A2%E3%83%AA).
- **Status Check**: All are "Temporarily removed," but since expiration is today, re-check GSC > Removals tool. If reverted, spam may reappear in reports.


### Solutions to Fix "Crawled - Currently Not Indexed"

Focus on root causes: Spam/hack, quality, and technical issues. Implement in phases: Clean, Prevent, Re-submit. I'll prioritize actionable steps.

#### 1. **Immediate Cleanup (Fix Spam and 403/Access Issues)**

- **Scan for Malware/Hacks**:
    - Use tools like Sucuri SiteCheck, Wordfence (if WordPress), or Malwarebytes. Check server logs for unauthorized access.
    - Update CMS (e.g., if WordPress, update to latest + plugins/themes). The "TeznevisanThemeX" paths suggest a custom theme â€“ disable/audit it for vulnerabilities.
    - Remove injected content: Delete spam files/pages via FTP/cPanel. Search for patterns like "?e=" in your database (e.g., via phpMyAdmin).
- **Handle 403 Pages**:
    - For examples like [https://teznevisan3.com/page/5/?_gl=](https://teznevisan3.com/page/5/?_gl=)... (403 instead of 404): Edit .htaccess or server config (e.g., Apache/Nginx) to return 404 or 410 (Gone) for these. Or add <meta name="robots" content="noindex"> to block indexing.
    - If dynamic, use robots.txt to disallow: e.g.,

```
User-agent: *
Disallow: /page/*?_gl=
Disallow: /?e=
Disallow: /public/themes/TeznevisanThemeX/
```

Test with GSC's Robots.txt Tester.
- **Noindex Low-Quality/Spam Pages**:
    - Add noindex meta tags or X-Robots-Tag headers to spam URLs (e.g., via .htaccess: `Header set X-Robots-Tag "noindex"` for matching patterns).
    - For bulk: Use GSC's URL Removal tool for temporary hides while cleaning (add missing patterns like ?e=, ?channel=).
- **Redirect or 404 Junk**:
    - 301 redirect spam to canonical pages (e.g., redirect ?e= URLs to homepage), or set to 404 to signal "gone."


#### 2. **Improve Content Quality and Site Structure**

- **Audit Content**: Focus on core pages (e.g., /writing-thesis, /research-methodology). Ensure unique, valuable content (e.g., 1000+ words, original academic advice). Remove duplicates.
- **Thin Content Fix**: If pages like /privacy-policy-2/ or /blog/statistical-analysis/ are short, expand them.
- **Internal Linking**: Link from high-quality pages to others to boost crawl priority.
- **Mobile-Friendly/Speed**: Test with GSC's Core Web Vitals and PageSpeed Insights. Fix if failing (common for non-indexing).
- **Schema Markup**: Add structured data (e.g., Article schema for blog posts) to signal quality.


#### 3. **Sitemap and Crawl Optimization**

- **Resubmit Sitemap**: Your metadata says "All known pages," but clean it first â€“ remove spam URLs from XML sitemap (generate via Yoast/All in One SEO if WP). Submit updated in GSC.
- **Fetch as Google**: Use GSC's URL Inspection tool on key URLs (e.g., https://teznevisan3.com/extracting-paper-from-dissertation/). Request indexing for up to 10/day.
- **Crawl Budget**: Reduce spam pages to free budget for good ones. Monitor in GSC > Settings > Crawl Stats.


#### 4. **Backlinks and External Signals**

- If spam URLs have bad backlinks, use GSC's Disavow tool (download backlinks from GSC > Links, disavow spammy domains).
- Build quality backlinks to core pages (e.g., guest posts on academic sites).


#### 5. **Monitoring and Long-Term Prevention**

- **GSC Alerts**: Enable email notifications for indexing issues.
- **Security**: Install firewall (e.g., Cloudflare), enable HTTPS, use strong passwords.
- **Re-Check in 2-4 Weeks**: After fixes, monitor GSC for shifts from "not indexed" to "Indexed."
- **If Hacked**: If confirmed, follow Google's hacked site guide (search "site hacked Google Search Console").

If these don't resolve, it could be a manual action (check GSC > Security \& Manual Actions). Provide more GSC exports (e.g., Coverage report) for deeper analysis. Start with cleanup â€“ that's the core issue here.
